The Disagreement over 'Aql: Genus or Species?
Explains the philosophical dispute over 'aql's classification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two main positions on the classification of 'aql and the implications for its individuals as either a genus with different species or a species with accidental differences.

Core Idea
Philosophers disagreed whether 'aql is a unique genus or a species, changing how substance is divided.

The passage begins by noting a disagreement among philosophers about whether the intellect ('aql) falls under a genus or not. This disagreement affects whether 'aql is a genus with different species or a single species with accidental differences. Understanding this debate is crucial for grasping the Peripatetic ontology of intellects.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disagreement
Locate the phrase indicating a difference of opinion about 'aql. Note the two options: Is 'aql included under a genus or not?
The phrase 'فيه إشعار بأن في المسألة خلافاً' signals the disagreement.
2
Analyze the two scenarios
If 'aql is not included under a genus, two possibilities: it is either a genus with species differing by differentiae (like 'animal') or a species with individuals differing by accidents (like 'man').
The examples of 'animal' and 'man' illustrate the distinction.
3
Connect to the example
The matn exemplifies one view, and later another view; understand why the author uses these examples.
This shows the author is aware of both positions.
4
Determine the underlying assumption
The debate assumes 'aql is not under a genus; what changes if it is? This leads to the division of substance into five types.
The next part of the passage explores the case where 'aql is under a genus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (بِنَاءً عَلَى أَنَّهُ جِنْسُ عِنْدَهُمْ) فيه إشعار بأنَّ في المسألة خلافاً . عندهم جنس وبيانُهُ : أنَّ الفلاسفة - قبَّحهم الله تعالى - اختلفوا أوَّلاً في العقل؛ هل هو داخل تحت أم لا؟ وعلى أنَّه ليس داخلاً فهل أفراده كأفراد الحَيَوَان؛ أي مختلفة بالحقيقة، فيكون هو جنساً منفرداً أفراده تختلف بالفصول، أو كأفراد الإنسان؛ أي: متفقة بالحقيقة، فيكون هو نوعاً منفرداً أفراده تختلف بالخواص؟ والتمثيل به هنا على القول الأول، ومثل به فيما يأتي ؛ بناءً على القول الثاني، وهذا كله مبني على أنَّه ليس بداخل تحت جنس، كما صرح بذلك الشَّارح ، أما على القول بأنَّه داخل تحت جنس، فقالوا : إنَّ الجوهر وهو ماهيَّةٌ إذا وجدت في الخارج كانت لا في موضوع كما مرَّ يدخل تحته خمسة أنواع ; لأنَّه إمَّا حال ويسمى : «الصُّورة»، كالصُّورة الإنسانية الواردة على النُّطفة، والرَّماديَّة الواردة على الحطب فيذهب اسم النُّطفة والحطب ومسمَّياهما، وبذلك لا تلتبس بالعرض ; لأنَّ العَرَض إنَّما يذهب معه الاسم كـ ثوب أبيض وردت عليه الحمرة أو بالعكس، فمسمَّى الثَّوب باقٍ ووصفه ذهب . وإما محل وهو الهَيُولى كالنُّطفة فيما تقدَّم، فالهَيُولى غير الموضوع; لأنَّ الموضوع لا يتغيَّر بما يرد عليه وإمَّا مركَّب منهما ; أي: مِنَ الحال والمحل، وهو الجسم كالسرير، فإنَّ صورته التأليف وهيولاه الخشب والمسامير، وهي المادة، أو لا حال ولا محلَّ وهو المجرَّد، وفيه قسمان; لأنَّه إمَّا أن يتعلَّق بالبدن تعلُّق التَّدبير والتّصريف وهو النَّفس، أو لا يتعلق به وهو العقل، فالعقلُ على قولهم جوهر مجرَّدُ عن المادة وعلائقها، وليس في حيز، وقالوا - لعنهم الله تعالى -: إنَّ صانع هذا العالم فاعلُ بالتَّعليل تعالى الله عن قولهم علوا كبيراً، وسموه: «عقلاً»، وهو العقل الأكبر عندهم، وسموه بـ «العقل» ; لأنَّه يدبر الأشياء، ثم قالوا : لا يصدر عنه إلا أربعة أمور: نفس الفلك، وصورة له، ومادة له، وعقل. ثمَّ هذا العقل الثَّاني يصدر عنه أربعة أخرى أيضاً كالأول، وهكذا الثَّالث إلى أن ذلك ينتهي إلى الـعـاشـر، ويـسـمـونـه ـ أي: العاشر - : «العقل الفعّال أو: «الفياض»; لأنَّه يفيض في زعمهم على العالم السفليّ [الكون و] الفساد ; أي : التَّغير - لعنهم الله تعالى وأخزاهم ، فهذه العقول العشرة هي المرادة بأفراد العقل. والحاصلُ : أنَّ هذا التَّقسيم مبني على القول بأنَّ العقل داخل تحت جنس كما قررنا، وأما على القول الآخر فالجوهر منقسم إلى الثَّلاثة الأول فقط مِنَ الأقسام الخمسة المتقدمة، وبه تعلم ما وقع لقدورة تبعاً لـ «نسج الحلل» من أنَّ الجنس عندهم هو الهَيُولى والصُّورة كالجوهر، مع أنهما قسمان من أقسام الجوهر، فيكونان مباينين على كلا المذهبين والحقُّ عند أهل السنة رضي الله تعالى عنهم أنَّ الجوهر إن لم يقبل القسمة فهو الفرد، وإلَّا فهو الجسم، وأنكروا ما عدا ذلك .
His statement: (built on the fact that it is a genus according to them) contains an indication that there is a difference of opinion in the issue. Its explanation is that the philosophers - may Allah curse them - differed first about the intellect: whether it is included under [a genus] or not? And assuming it is not included, are its individuals like the individuals of 'animal', i.e., different in reality, so it is an independent genus whose individuals differ by differentiae, or like the individuals of 'man', i.e., agreeing in reality, so it is an independent species whose individuals differ by properties? The exemplification here is on the first opinion, and it was exemplified later based on the second opinion. All this is built on it not being included under a genus, as the commentator stated. As for the opinion that it is included under a genus, they said: substance (jawhar) - which is a quiddity that when found externally is not in a subject - includes under it five types: because it is either a form (sura), like the human form received by the sperm and the ash form received by wood, so the name and its named entity disappear, and thus it is not confused with accident; because the accident only causes the name to go away, like a white cloth upon which redness comes, so the named entity (cloth) remains but its description goes. Or it is matter (hayula), like the sperm in the previous example, so hayula is not the subject because the subject does not change with what comes upon it. Or it is composed of both (form and matter), which is body (jism), like a bed, its form is the arrangement and its hayula is wood and nails. Or it is neither form nor matter: the abstract (mujarrad), and it has two divisions: either it is related to the body by way of management and disposal, which is the soul (nafs), or not related, which is the intellect ('aql). The intellect, according to them, is an abstract substance free from matter and its attachments, not in a location. And they said - may Allah curse them - that the Maker of this world is an agent by causation, exalted is Allah above their saying greatly, and they called it 'aql, and it is the greatest intellect according to them. Then they said: nothing emanates from it except four things: the soul of the sphere, its form, its matter, and an intellect. Then this second intellect emanates another four as well, and so on until the tenth, which they call the active intellect or the outpouring one, because it pours upon the world of generation and corruption. So these ten intellects are meant by the individuals of 'aql. The conclusion: this division is based on the opinion that 'aql is included under a genus, as we stated. According to the other opinion, substance is divided only into the first three of the five divisions mentioned. And by this you know what happened to Qudura following 'Nasj al-Hulal' that the genus according to them is hayula and form like substance, while they are two divisions of substance, so they would be distinct on both views. The truth according to the People of the Sunna is that substance if it does not accept division is the atom, otherwise it is body, and they denied what is beyond that.
Source pages p. 520

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a line from the matn that says 'based on it being a genus according to them'. The commentator explains that this phrase indicates a disagreement among philosophers about the intellect ('aql). They differed on whether 'aql is included under a genus (like substance) or not. If it is not included, then it could be a genus with species differing by differentiae, or a species with individuals differing by accidents. The example given in the matn corresponds to the first view, while another example elsewhere corresponds to the second. If it is included under a genus, then substance is divided into five types: form, matter, composite (body), and two types of abstract (soul and intellect). These correspond to the standard Peripatetic division. The author then describes the Neoplatonic emanation scheme of ten intellects, which he criticizes as false. He concludes with the correct Sunni view: substance is either the atom (al-fard) or the body. This shows the theological critique of Aristotelian metaphysics.

Key Terms
عقل
جنس
نوع
فصل
خاصة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if 'aql is not under a genus, what are the two possibilities for its classification?
A) It is a genus with species differing by differentiae, or a species with individuals differing by accidents.
B) It is an accident or a substance.
C) It is a body or a soul.
D) It is an atom or a composite.

Key Takeaway
The classification of 'aql hinges on whether it falls under a higher genus, leading to two distinct ontological schemes.

The Five Types of Substance in Peripatetic Philosophy
Presents the Peripatetic division of substance into five types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the five types of substance according to the Peripatetic philosophers and explain the rationale for each.

Core Idea
Substance is divided into form, matter, body, soul, and intellect, each with a precise definition.

When philosophers consider substance as a genus, they divide it into five types: form, matter, body, soul, and intellect. This division is based on whether the substance is form, matter, composite, or abstract, and whether it is related to the body or not. This systematic classification underlies their entire physical and metaphysical worldview.

Guided Path
1
Identify the genus being divided
Recognize that substance (jawhar) is the genus under which these five types fall.
The passage starts with 'أما على القول بأنه داخل تحت جنس'
2
Understand the primary division
Note that substance is either form (sura), matter (hayula), composite (body), or abstract (mujarrad).
The abstract includes soul and intellect.
3
Distinguish the two abstract types
Abstract is divided into soul (nafs) which manages the body, and intellect ('aql) which is not attached.
This distinction is crucial for the emanation scheme later.
4
Memorize the five and their definitions
Form is the organizing principle; matter is the underlying substrate; body is their composite; soul is the abstract managing the body; intellect is the abstract not managing.
Examples: human form in sperm, wood for matter, bed for body.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (بِنَاءً عَلَى أَنَّهُ جِنْسُ عِنْدَهُمْ) فيه إشعار بأنَّ في المسألة خلافاً . عندهم جنس وبيانُهُ : أنَّ الفلاسفة - قبَّحهم الله تعالى - اختلفوا أوَّلاً في العقل؛ هل هو داخل تحت أم لا؟ وعلى أنَّه ليس داخلاً فهل أفراده كأفراد الحَيَوَان؛ أي مختلفة بالحقيقة، فيكون هو جنساً منفرداً أفراده تختلف بالفصول، أو كأفراد الإنسان؛ أي: متفقة بالحقيقة، فيكون هو نوعاً منفرداً أفراده تختلف بالخواص؟ والتمثيل به هنا على القول الأول، ومثل به فيما يأتي ؛ بناءً على القول الثاني، وهذا كله مبني على أنَّه ليس بداخل تحت جنس، كما صرح بذلك الشَّارح ، أما على القول بأنَّه داخل تحت جنس، فقالوا : إنَّ الجوهر وهو ماهيَّةٌ إذا وجدت في الخارج كانت لا في موضوع كما مرَّ يدخل تحته خمسة أنواع ; لأنَّ الموضوع لا يتغيَّر بما يرد عليه وإمَّا مركَّب منهما ; أي: مِنَ الحال والمحل، وهو الجسم كالسرير، فإنَّ صورته التأليف وهيولاه الخشب والمسامير، وهي المادة، أو لا حال ولا محلَّ وهو المجرَّد، وفيه قسمان; His statement: (built on the fact that it is a genus according to them) contains an indication that there is a difference of opinion in the issue. Its explanation is that the philosophers - may Allah curse them - differed first about the intellect: whether it is included under [a genus] or not? And assuming it is not included, are its individuals like the individuals of 'animal', i.e., different in reality, so it is an independent genus whose individuals differ by differentiae, or like the individuals of 'man', i.e., agreeing in reality, so it is an independent species whose individuals differ by properties? The exemplification here is on the first opinion, and it was exemplified later based on the second opinion. All this is built on it not being included under a genus, as the commentator stated. As for the opinion that it is included under a genus, they said: substance (jawhar) - which is a quiddity that when found externally is not in a subject - includes under it five types: because it is either a form (sura), like the human form received by the sperm and the ash form received by wood, so the name and its named entity disappear, and thus it is not confused with accident; because the accident only causes the name to go away, like a white cloth upon which redness comes, so the named entity (cloth) remains but its description goes. Or it is matter (hayula), like the sperm in the previous example, so hayula is not the subject because the subject does not change with what comes upon it. Or it is composed of both (form and matter), which is body (jism), like a bed, its form is the arrangement and its hayula is wood and nails. Or it is neither form nor matter: the abstract (mujarrad), and it has two divisions: either it is related to the body by way of management and disposal, which is the soul (nafs), or not related, which is the intellect ('aql). The intellect, according to them, is an abstract substance free from matter and its attachments, not in a location. And they said - may Allah curse them - that the Maker of this world is an agent by causation, exalted is Allah above their saying greatly, and they called it 'aql, and it is the greatest intellect according to them. Then they said: nothing emanates from it except four things: the soul of the sphere, its form, its matter, and an intellect. Then this second intellect emanates another four as well, and so on until the tenth, which they call the active intellect or the outpouring one, because it pours upon the world of generation and corruption. So these ten intellects are meant by the individuals of 'aql. The conclusion: this division is based on the opinion that 'aql is included under a genus, as we stated. According to the other opinion, substance is divided only into the first three of the five divisions mentioned. And by this you know what happened to Qudura following 'Nasj al-Hulal' that the genus according to them is hayula and form like substance, while they are two divisions of substance, so they would be distinct on both views. The truth according to the People of the Sunna is that substance if it does not accept division is the atom, otherwise it is body, and they denied what is beyond that.
Source pages p. 520

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a line from the matn that says 'based on it being a genus according to them'. The commentator explains that this phrase indicates a disagreement among philosophers about the intellect ('aql). They differed on whether 'aql is included under a genus (like substance) or not. If it is not included, then it could be a genus with species differing by differentiae, or a species with individuals differing by accidents. The example given in the matn corresponds to the first view, while another example elsewhere corresponds to the second. If it is included under a genus, then substance is divided into five types: form, matter, composite (body), and two types of abstract (soul and intellect). These correspond to the standard Peripatetic division. The author then describes the Neoplatonic emanation scheme of ten intellects, which he criticizes as false. He concludes with the correct Sunni view: substance is either the atom (al-fard) or the body. This shows the theological critique of Aristotelian metaphysics.

نفس

Key Takeaway
The Peripatetic division of substance into five types provides a framework for understanding all existing entities, but it is rejected by Sunni theologians.

Refutation of the Philosophers' Emanation Scheme
Critiques the philosophers' emanation of ten intellects and provides Sunni alternative.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to outline the philosophers' emanation scheme of ten intellects and explain the Sunni theological critique.

Core Idea
The philosophers' ten intellects are built on false premises; the Sunni view simplifies substance to atom or body.

After dividing substance, the philosophers propose an emanation scheme where the First Intellect emanates a second, and so on, up to ten intellects. The author explicitly condemns this as false and presents the Sunni alternative: substance is either the indivisible atom (al-fard) or the composite body. This lesson examines both the scheme and its critique.

Guided Path
1
Understand the emanation starting point
The philosophers claim the First Intellect (the Creator) emanates four things: soul of sphere, its form, its matter, and another intellect.
This is the Neoplatonic principle of emanation.
2
Follow the chain
Each subsequent intellect emanates four more, continuing until the tenth (active intellect).
The chain ends at the active intellect, which influences the sublunary world.
3
Identify the role of the active intellect
It is said to pour upon the world of generation and corruption, explaining natural change.
This is supposed to explain the origin of forms in the material world.
4
Analyze the Sunni refutation
The Sunni view rejects all these distinctions, defining substance simply as either atom or body.
The author curses the philosophers and states the Sunni position as the truth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (بِنَاءً عَلَى أَنَّهُ جِنْسُ عِنْدَهُمْ) فيه إشعار بأنَّ في المسألة خلافاً . عندهم جنس وبيانُهُ : أنَّ الفلاسفة - قبَّحهم الله تعالى - اختلفوا أوَّلاً في العقل؛ هل هو داخل تحت أم لا؟ وعلى أنَّه ليس داخلاً فهل أفراده كأفراد الحَيَوَان؛ أي مختلفة بالحقيقة، فيكون هو جنساً منفرداً أفراده تختلف بالفصول، أو كأفراد الإنسان؛ أي: متفقة بالحقيقة، فيكون هو نوعاً منفرداً أفراده تختلف بالخواص؟ والتمثيل به هنا على القول الأول، ومثل به فيما يأتي ؛ بناءً على القول الثاني، وهذا كله مبني على أنَّه ليس بداخل تحت جنس، كما صرح بذلك الشَّارح ، أما على القول بأنَّه داخل تحت جنس، فقالوا : إنَّ الجوهر وهو ماهيَّةٌ إذا وجدت في الخارج كانت لا في موضوع كما مرَّ يدخل تحته خمسة أنواع ; لأنَّه إمَّا حال ويسمى : «الصُّورة»، كالصُّورة الإنسانية الواردة على النُّطفة، والرَّماديَّة الواردة على الحطب فيذهب اسم النُّطفة والحطب ومسمَّياهما، وبذلك لا تلتبس بالعرض ; لأنَّ العَرَض إنَّما يذهب معه الاسم كـ ثوب أبيض وردت عليه الحمرة أو بالعكس، فمسمَّى الثَّوب باقٍ ووصفه ذهب . وإما محل وهو الهَيُولى كالنُّطفة فيما تقدَّم، فالهَيُولى غير الموضوع; لأنَّ الموضوع لا يتغيَّر بما يرد عليه وإمَّا مركَّب منهما ; أي: مِنَ الحال والمحل، وهو الجسم كالسرير، فإنَّ صورته التأليف وهيولاه الخشب والمسامير، وهي المادة، أو لا حال ولا محلَّ وهو المجرَّد، وفيه قسمان; لأنَّه إمَّا أن يتعلَّق بالبدن تعلُّق التَّدبير والتّصريف وهو النَّفس، أو لا يتعلق به وهو العقل، فالعقلُ على قولهم جوهر مجرَّدُ عن المادة وعلائقها، وليس في حيز، وقالوا - لعنهم الله تعالى -: إنَّ صانع هذا العالم فاعلُ بالتَّعليل تعالى الله عن قولهم علوا كبيراً، وسموه: «عقلاً»، وهو العقل الأكبر عندهم، وسموه بـ «العقل» ; لأنَّه يدبر الأشياء، ثم قالوا : لا يصدر عنه إلا أربعة أمور: نفس الفلك، وصورة له، ومادة له، وعقل. ثمَّ هذا العقل الثَّاني يصدر عنه أربعة أخرى أيضاً كالأول، وهكذا الثَّالث إلى أن ذلك ينتهي إلى الـعـاشـر، ويـسـمـونـه ـ أي: العاشر - : «العقل الفعّال أو: «الفياض»; لأنَّه يفيض في زعمهم على العالم السفليّ [الكون و] الفساد ; أي : التَّغير - لعنهم الله تعالى وأخزاهم ، فهذه العقول العشرة هي المرادة بأفراد العقل. والحاصلُ : أنَّ هذا التَّقسيم مبني على القول بأنَّ العقل داخل تحت جنس كما قررنا، وأما على القول الآخر فالجوهر منقسم إلى الثَّلاثة الأول فقط مِنَ الأقسام الخمسة المتقدمة، وبه تعلم ما وقع لقدورة تبعاً لـ «نسج الحلل» من أنَّ الجنس عندهم هو الهَيُولى والصُّورة كالجوهر، مع أنهما قسمان من أقسام الجوهر، فيكونان مباينين على كلا المذهبين والحقُّ عند أهل السنة رضي الله تعالى عنهم أنَّ الجوهر إن لم يقبل القسمة فهو الفرد، وإلَّا فهو الجسم، وأنكروا ما عدا ذلك .
His statement: (built on the fact that it is a genus according to them) contains an indication that there is a difference of opinion in the issue. Its explanation is that the philosophers - may Allah curse them - differed first about the intellect: whether it is included under [a genus] or not? And assuming it is not included, are its individuals like the individuals of 'animal', i.e., different in reality, so it is an independent genus whose individuals differ by differentiae, or like the individuals of 'man', i.e., agreeing in reality, so it is an independent species whose individuals differ by properties? The exemplification here is on the first opinion, and it was exemplified later based on the second opinion. All this is built on it not being included under a genus, as the commentator stated. As for the opinion that it is included under a genus, they said: substance (jawhar) - which is a quiddity that when found externally is not in a subject - includes under it five types: because it is either a form (sura), like the human form received by the sperm and the ash form received by wood, so the name and its named entity disappear, and thus it is not confused with accident; because the accident only causes the name to go away, like a white cloth upon which redness comes, so the named entity (cloth) remains but its description goes. Or it is matter (hayula), like the sperm in the previous example, so hayula is not the subject because the subject does not change with what comes upon it. Or it is composed of both (form and matter), which is body (jism), like a bed, its form is the arrangement and its hayula is wood and nails. Or it is neither form nor matter: the abstract (mujarrad), and it has two divisions: either it is related to the body by way of management and disposal, which is the soul (nafs), or not related, which is the intellect ('aql). The intellect, according to them, is an abstract substance free from matter and its attachments, not in a location. And they said - may Allah curse them - that the Maker of this world is an agent by causation, exalted is Allah above their saying greatly, and they called it 'aql, and it is the greatest intellect according to them. Then they said: nothing emanates from it except four things: the soul of the sphere, its form, its matter, and an intellect. Then this second intellect emanates another four as well, and so on until the tenth, which they call the active intellect or the outpouring one, because it pours upon the world of generation and corruption. So these ten intellects are meant by the individuals of 'aql. The conclusion: this division is based on the opinion that 'aql is included under a genus, as we stated. According to the other opinion, substance is divided only into the first three of the five divisions mentioned. And by this you know what happened to Qudura following 'Nasj al-Hulal' that the genus according to them is hayula and form like substance, while they are two divisions of substance, so they would be distinct on both views. The truth according to the People of the Sunna is that substance if it does not accept division is the atom, otherwise it is body, and they denied what is beyond that.

This passage is a commentary on a line from the matn that says 'based on it being a genus according to them'. The commentator explains that this phrase indicates a disagreement among philosophers about the intellect ('aql). They differed on whether 'aql is included under a genus (like substance) or not. He concludes with the correct Sunni view: substance is either the atom (al-fard) or the body. This shows the theological critique of Aristotelian metaphysics.

Divisions of Substance in Islamic Logic
Bajuri-Bannani defines the divisions of substance and refutes the philosophers' ten intellects

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify substances according to the logicians' division and identify the Ash'ari position on substance.

Core Idea
Substance is either body (divisible) or atom (indivisible) – the only two real categories.

In this passage, al-Bajuri lays out the logical division of substance (jawhar) as understood by the philosophers and then presents the orthodox Ash'ari view. Understanding this division is crucial for distinguishing between material and immaterial entities in theological discourse.

Guided Path
1
Identify two types of change
The passage distinguishes change 'by accident' (attribute changes, substance remains) and change 'by matter' (substrate changes). Notice which remains constant in each.
Example: white cloth becoming red is accidental change; sperm developing is material change.
2
Extract classification of substance
Substance is divided into composed (form+matter = body) and abstract (soul/intellect). Abstract is further divided into soul (related to body) and intellect (completely separate).
The philosophers consider intellect as a separate substance.
3
Identify the Ash'ari view
The author states: 'The truth according to Ahl al-Sunna is that substance if it does not accept division is the atom, otherwise it is the body, and they denied what is beyond that.'
This simplifies the division to just two types: atom (al-fard) and body (al-jism).
4
Recognize rejection of extra categories
The philosophers' ten intellects are rejected; they do not count as substances in the Ash'ari framework.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في مباحث الألفاظ
وَقَدْ عَلِمْتَ المُغَايَرَةَ بَيْنَهُمَا مَفْهُوماً وَمَصْدُوقاً .
بالعرض ؛ لأنَّ العَرَض إنَّما يذهب معه الاسم كـ ثوب أبيض وردت عليه الحمرة أو بالعكس، فمسمَّى الثَّوب باقٍ ووصفه ذهب .
وإما محل وهو الهَيُولى كالنُّطفة فيما تقدَّم، فالهَيُولى غير الموضوع؛ لأنَّ الموضوع لا يتغيَّر بما يرد عليه وإمَّا مركَّب منهما ؛ أي: مِنَ الحال والمحل، وهو الجسم كالسرير، فإنَّ صورته التأليف وهيولاه الخشب والمسامير، وهي المادة، أو لا حال ولا محلَّ وهو المجرَّد، وفيه قسمان؛ لأنَّه إما أن يتعلَّق بالبدن تعلُّق التَّدبير والتّصريف وهو النَّفس، أو لا يتعلق به وهو العقل، فالعقلُ على قولهم جوهر مجرَّدُ عن المادة وعلائقها، وليس في حيز، وقالوا - لعنهم الله تعالى -: إنَّ صانع هذا العالم فاعلُ بالتَّعليل تعالى الله عن قولهم علوا كبيراً، وسموه: «عقلاً»، وهو العقل الأكبر عندهم، وسموه بـ «العقل» ; لأنَّه يدبر الأشياء، ثم قالوا : لا يصدر عنه إلا أربعة أمور: نفس الفلك، وصورة له، ومادة له، وعقل. ثمَّ هذا العقل الثَّاني يصدر عنه أربعة أخرى أيضاً كالأول، وهكذا الثَّالث إلى أن ذلك ينتهي إلى الـعـاشـر، ويـسـمـونـه ـ أي: العاشر - : «العقل الفعّال أو: «الفياض»; لأنَّه يفيض في زعمهم على العالم السفليّ [الكون و] الفساد ; أي : التَّغير - لعنهم الله تعالى وأخزاهم ، فهذه العقول العشرة هي المرادة بأفراد العقل.
والحاصلُ : أنَّ هذا التَّقسيم مبني على القول بأنَّ العقل داخل تحت جنس كما قررنا، وأما على القول الآخر فالجوهر منقسم إلى الثَّلاثة الأول فقط مِنَ الأقسام الخمسة المتقدمة، وبه تعلم ما وقع لقدورة تبعاً لـ «نسج الحلل» من أنَّ الجنس عندهم هو الهَيُولى والصُّورة كالجوهر، مع أنهما قسمان من أقسام الجوهر، فيكونان مباينين على كلا المذهبين والحقُّ عند أهل السنة رضي الله تعالى عنهم أنَّ الجوهر إن لم يقبل القسمة فهو الفرد، وإلَّا فهو الجسم، وأنكروا ما عدا ذلك .
Section on topics of words. And you have known the difference between them in concept and referent. By accident, because the accident only takes away the name, like a white cloth that receives redness or vice versa, so the named cloth remains and its attribute goes. Or it is a place which is matter, like the sperm in what preceded, for matter is not subject; because the subject does not change by what occurs to it. Or it is composed of both, i.e., of the state and the place, which is the body, like a bed, for its form is the arrangement and its matter is wood and nails, which is material. Or there is no state and no place, which is the abstract, and it has two divisions; because it either relates to the body by relation of management and disposition, which is the soul, or does not relate to it, which is the intellect. So the intellect according to them is a substance abstract from matter and its attachments, and not in a place. And they said - may Allah curse them - that the Maker of this world is an agent by causation, exalted is Allah above their saying greatly, and they called it 'intellect', and it is the greatest intellect according to them, and they called it 'intellect' because it manages things. Then they said: nothing issues from it except four things: the soul of the sphere, a form for it, a matter for it, and an intellect. Then this second intellect also issues four others like the first, and so the third until that ends at the tenth, and they call it - i.e., the tenth - 'the active intellect' or 'the effusive', because it effuses in their claim upon the lower world of generation and corruption, i.e., change - may Allah curse them and disgrace them. So these ten intellects are intended as individuals of intellect. And the conclusion: that this division is based on the statement that the intellect falls under a genus as we established. And on the other statement, substance is divided into only the first three of the five divisions mentioned. And by this you know what occurred for Qadurah following 'Nasj al-Hilal' that the genus according to them is matter and form like substance, while they are two divisions of substance, so they are distinct on both schools. The truth according to Ahl al-Sunna, may Allah be pleased with them, is that substance if it does not accept division is the atom, otherwise it is the body, and they denied what is beyond that.
Source pages p. 521

Commentary
This passage is a critical exposition of the division of substance (jawhar) according to the philosophers, followed by the orthodox refutation. The author begins by distinguishing between two types of change: 'by accident' where the attribute changes but the substance remains (e.g., a white cloth becoming red), and 'by matter' where the underlying matter changes (e.g., sperm developing). He then classifies substances into those composed of form and matter (bodies like a bed), those that are abstract without matter, and further divides the abstract into soul (related to body) and intellect (completely separate). The author then launches a vehement critique of the philosophers' doctrine of ten intellects emanating from the First Intellect, which they identify with God. He curses them for this causal emanationism. The conclusion is that this whole scheme is based on the assumption that intellect is a species under a genus, which the author rejects. He asserts the Ash'ari view that substance either is indivisible (al-fard, the atom) or divisible (al-jism, the body), and denies any other divisions.

الجوهر
الهيولى
العقل

A) Composed and abstract
B) Atom and body
C) Matter and form
D) Soul and intellect

Key Takeaway
In Islamic theology, substance (jawhar) is strictly either an indivisible atom (al-fard) or a divisible body (al-jism).

Refutation of the Philosophers' Ten Intellects
Bajuri-Bannani defines the divisions of substance and refutes the philosophers' ten intellects

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the philosophers' emanation scheme of ten intellects and explain the theological grounds for its refutation by Ahl al-Sunna.

Core Idea
The ten intellects are a Greek emanation scheme rejected by Ahl al-Sunna as false causation attributed to God.

In this passage, al-Bajuri presents the philosophers' doctrine of ten intellects emanating from the First Intellect (God), then vehemently curses them and asserts the Ash'ari position. This illustrates how logical categories can be used to construct metaphysical systems conflicting with Islamic orthodoxy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the philosophers' starting point
They claim the Maker (God) acts by causation (fa'il bil-ta'lil). They call the First Intellect 'intellect' because it manages things.
2
Describe the first emanation
From the First Intellect issue four things: the soul of the sphere, a form for the sphere, a matter for the sphere, and another intellect (the second).
Each emanation produces a soul, a form, a matter, and an intellect.
3
Follow the chain to ten intellects
Each subsequent intellect similarly emits four until the tenth intellect, called the active intellect (al-'aql al-fa''al), which governs the sublunar world of generation and corruption.
4
Note the author's condemnation
The author intersperses curses ('may Allah curse them', 'exalted is Allah above their saying') showing this doctrine is not accepted.
5
Learn the Ash'ari corrective
The author concludes that substance is either atom or body, denying these separate intellects as substances.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في مباحث الألفاظ
وَقَدْ عَلِمْتَ المُغَايَرَةَ بَيْنَهُمَا مَفْهُوماً وَمَصْدُوقاً .
بالعرض ؛ لأنَّ العَرَض إنَّما يذهب معه الاسم كـ ثوب أبيض وردت عليه الحمرة أو بالعكس، فمسمَّى الثَّوب باقٍ ووصفه ذهب .
وإما محل وهو الهَيُولى كالنُّطفة فيما تقدَّم، فالهَيُولى غير الموضوع؛ لأنَّ الموضوع لا يتغيَّر بما يرد عليه وإمَّا مركَّب منهما ؛ أي: مِنَ الحال والمحل، وهو الجسم كالسرير، فإنَّ صورته التأليف وهيولاه الخشب والمسامير، وهي المادة، أو لا حال ولا محلَّ وهو المجرَّد، وفيه قسمان؛ لأنَّه إما أن يتعلَّق بالبدن تعلُّق التَّدبير والتّصريف وهو النَّفس، أو لا يتعلق به وهو العقل، فالعقلُ على قولهم جوهر مجرَّدُ عن المادة وعلائقها، وليس في حيز، وقالوا - لعنهم الله تعالى -: إنَّ صانع هذا العالم فاعلُ بالتَّعليل تعالى الله عن قولهم علوا كبيراً، وسموه: «عقلاً»، وهو العقل الأكبر عندهم، وسموه بـ «العقل» ; لأنَّه يدبر الأشياء، ثم قالوا : لا يصدر عنه إلا أربعة أمور: نفس الفلك، وصورة له، ومادة له، وعقل. ثمَّ هذا العقل الثَّاني يصدر عنه أربعة أخرى أيضاً كالأول، وهكذا الثَّالث إلى أن ذلك ينتهي إلى الـعـاشـر، ويـسـمـونـه ـ أي: العاشر - : «العقل الفعّال أو: «الفياض»; لأنَّه يفيض في زعمهم على العالم السفليّ [الكون و] الفساد ; أي : التَّغير - لعنهم الله تعالى وأخزاهم ، فهذه العقول العشرة هي المرادة بأفراد العقل.
والحاصلُ : أنَّ هذا التَّقسيم مبني على القول بأنَّ العقل داخل تحت جنس كما قررنا، وأما على القول الآخر فالجوهر منقسم إلى الثَّلاثة الأول فقط مِنَ الأقسام الخمسة المتقدمة، وبه تعلم ما وقع لقدورة تبعاً لـ «نسج الحلل» من أنَّ الجنس عندهم هو الهَيُولى والصُّورة كالجوهر، مع أنهما قسمان من أقسام الجوهر، فيكونان مباينين على كلا المذهبين والحقُّ عند أهل السنة رضي الله تعالى عنهم أنَّ الجوهر إن لم يقبل القسمة فهو الفرد، وإلَّا فهو الجسم، وأنكروا ما عدا ذلك .
Section on topics of words. And you have known the difference between them in concept and referent. By accident, because the accident only takes away the name, like a white cloth that receives redness or vice versa, so the named cloth remains and its attribute goes. Or it is a place which is matter, like the sperm in what preceded, for matter is not subject; because the subject does not change by what occurs to it. Or it is composed of both, i.e., of the state and the place, which is the body, like a bed, for its form is the arrangement and its matter is wood and nails, which is material. Or there is no state and no place, which is the abstract, and it has two divisions; because it either relates to the body by relation of management and disposition, which is the soul, or does not relate to it, which is the intellect. So the intellect according to them is a substance abstract from matter and its attachments, and not in a place. And they said - may Allah curse them - that the Maker of this world is an agent by causation, exalted is Allah above their saying greatly, and they called it 'intellect', and it is the greatest intellect according to them, and they called it 'intellect' because it manages things. Then they said: nothing issues from it except four things: the soul of the sphere, a form for it, a matter for it, and an intellect. Then this second intellect also issues four others like the first, and so the third until that ends at the tenth, and they call it - i.e., the tenth - 'the active intellect' or 'the effusive', because it effuses in their claim upon the lower world of generation and corruption, i.e., change - may Allah curse them and disgrace them. So these ten intellects are intended as individuals of intellect. And the conclusion: that this division is based on the statement that the intellect falls under a genus as we established. And on the other statement, substance is divided into only the first three of the five divisions mentioned. And by this you know what occurred for Qadurah following 'Nasj al-Hilal' that the genus according to them is matter and form like substance, while they are two divisions of substance, so they are distinct on both schools. The truth according to Ahl al-Sunna, may Allah be pleased with them, is that substance if it does not accept division is the atom, otherwise it is the body, and they denied what is beyond that.
Source pages p. 521

Commentary
This passage is a critical exposition of the division of substance (jawhar) according to the philosophers, followed by the orthodox refutation. The author begins by distinguishing between two types of change: 'by accident' where the attribute changes but the substance remains (e.g., a white cloth becoming red), and 'by matter' where the underlying matter changes (e.g., sperm developing). He then classifies substances into those composed of form and matter (bodies like a bed), those that are abstract without matter, and further divides the abstract into soul (related to body) and intellect (completely separate). The author then launches a vehement critique of the philosophers' doctrine of ten intellects emanating from the First Intellect, which they identify with God. He curses them for this causal emanationism. The conclusion is that this whole scheme is based on the assumption that intellect is a species under a genus, which the author rejects. He asserts the Ash'ari view that substance either is indivisible (al-fard, the atom) or divisible (al-jism, the body), and denies any other divisions.

Key Terms
العقل
الفاعل بالتَّعليل
العقل الفعّال

Key Takeaway
The critique of the ten intellects shows that not all logical classifications are theologically acceptable; the Ash'ari position reduces substance to atom or body.

The Seven Necessary Propositions
Author enumerates and defines the seven necessary propositions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the seven types of necessary propositions (ḍarūriyya) by their temporal and conditional restrictions, and correctly classify any given example.

Core Idea
Necessary propositions are the strongest modality, with seven subtypes defined by absolute, conditional, temporal, and distributed restrictions.

In Islamic logic, modal propositions are classified by the strength and duration of their truth. The strongest are the necessary propositions (ḍarūriyya), which assert that the judgment must hold under specific conditions. This lesson unpacks the seven types explained in the source, from the absolute necessary to the distributed necessary, each with its distinct restriction and example. Mastering these will sharpen your ability to analyze the modality of any proposition in a syllogistic context.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overall category of necessary propositions
In the source text, after the chapter heading, the author lists the seven necessary propositions. Locate them and note that they are all labeled as 'ḍarūriyya' (ضرورية).
2
Extract the restriction for each subtype
For each of the seven types, identify the specific restriction: absolute (no restriction), conditional general (perpetuity of description), conditional special (perpetuity with negation at departure), temporal (specific time), temporal non-described (specific time with negation of perpetuity), absolute distributed (indefinite time), and distributed non-described (indefinite time with further restriction).
3
Note the examples provided
The source gives examples for each type, such as 'Every writer moves his fingers as long as he writes' for the general conditional. Write down each example and verify that it matches the restriction.
4
Compare the two conditional types and the two temporal types
Observe the difference between the general and special conditional: the special conditional explicitly negates perpetuity when the description departs. Similarly, the temporal types differ by whether they include a negation of perpetuity.
5
Understand the difference between specific time and indefinite time
The temporal types restrict the judgment to a specific time (like 'at the time of writing'), while the distributed types use an indefinite time ('at some time'). This distinction is crucial for syllogistic reasoning.

٥ - والوقتية غير الموصوفة بإطلاق مثلها، لكن مع التعرض لنفي الدوام.
٦ - والمنتشرة المطلقة كالوقتيَّة إلَّا أنَّ الوقت فيها غير معيَّن؛ نحو: كلُّ ممكن معدوم بالضرورة وقتاً ما» .
- والمنتشرة غير الموصوفة بإطلاق مثلها، لكن مع التقييد، فهذه الضروريات السبع؛ الأولى مطلقة والمشروطتان مقيَّدتان بدوام الوصف والوقتيَّتان بوقت معيَّن، والمنتشرتان بوقت مبهم . وأما الدوائم :
۱ - فالدائمة المطلقة ؛ نحو: «كل فلك متحرك دائماً».
٢ - والعرفية العامة : «ما قيد دوامها بوصف الموضوع من غير تعرض لنفي الدوام عند مفارقة ذلك الوصف»؛ نحو: كلُّ آكل متحرك الفكِّ الأسفل ما دام أكلاً»، سميت: «عرفيَّة؛ للاكتفاء في دوام نسبتها بالعرف والعادة، وإن لم يقتض العقل دوامها، كما في المثال المذكور، وعامَّةٌ ; لأَنَّها أَعمُّ مِنَ الَّتي بعدها . - والعرفيَّةُ الخاصة مثلها مع التّقييد ; فأمثلةُ الضَّروريّات الثَّلاث الأُوَل إن حذف منها لفظ الضرورة ، صارت أمثلة للدوائم الثلاث على الترتيب.
فهذه الدَّوائم الثَّلاث : الأولى ،مطلقة، والعرفيَّتان مقيَّدتان بدوام الوصف.
وأما المطلقات :
۱ - فالمطلقة العامة ؛ نحو: كلُّ إنسان ميت بالإطلاق العام».
۲ - والمطلقة الوجوديَّة اللا ضروريَّة وهي : المحكوم فيها بفعليَّة النسبة مع التقييد بنفي الضرورة ; نحو: كلُّ إنسان فهو ميت لا بالضَّرورة»، سمّيت : «وجوديَّة؛ لوجود نسبتها بالفعل، و: «لا ضروريَّة; لتقييدها بنفي الضرورة.
٣ - والوجودية اللا دائمة مثلها مع التقييد بنفي التقييد بنفي الدوام ; نحو: «كل إنسان حي لا دائماً». ٤ - والمطلقة الحينيَّة هي : التي قيَّدت نسبتها الفعليَّة بحين وصف الموضوع»; نحو: كلُّ كاتب متحرك الأصابع بالإطلاق حين هو كاتب.
والفرقُ بين التَّقييد بحين وصف الموضوع والتَّقييد بدوام وصفه : أنَّ التَّقييد بحين الوصف لا يستغرق جميع أحيانه، بخلاف دوام الوصف يستغرق جميع أحيان وصف الموضوع، وبهذا تعرف الفرق بين العرفيّة العامة وبين المطلقة الحينيَّة من حيث القيد.
فهذه المطلقات الأربع الأولى منهنَّ مطلقة، والثَّلاث بعدها مقيدات بنفي الدوام، ونفي الضّرورة، وبحين وصف الموضوع. وأما الممكنات :
۱ - فالممكنة العامة; نحو: كلُّ إنسانٍ حَيَوَان بالإمكان العام ; لأنَّ المراد بها ما نسبتها غير ممتنعة .
٢ - والممكنة الخاصة : ما حكم فيها بأنَّ نسبتها غير ممتنعة ولا ضرورية، بل جائزة مستوية الطَّرفين»; نحو: كلُّ جرم متحرك بالإمكان الخاص»، سمّيت : «ممكنة»; لأنَّ جهتها إمكان، و «خاصَّةٌ» ; لاختصاصها بمستوي الطرفين، فلا تصدق بالضَّرورة، بخلاف العامة.
٣ - والممكنة الوقتيّة هي: التي قيَّد إمكانها بوقت معيَّن»; نحو: كلُّ إنسان ميت بالإمكان العام وقت مفارقة الرُّوح له سمّيت ممكنةً» لما سبق، ووقتيَّةٌ»; لتقييد جهة إمكانها بوقت معيَّن . ٤ - والممكنة الحينيَّة وهي : التي قيَّد إمكانها بحين وصف الموضوع»; نحو: «كل آكل جائع بالإمكان حين هو آكل».
ه - والممكنة الدائمة: «الَّتي حكم فيها بدوام الإمكان»; نحو: كلُّ ممكن معدوم بالإمكان دائماً .
فهذه الممكنات الخمس ; الأولى منهنَّ مطلقة، والأربع بعدها مقيَّدة; إما بخصوص الإمكان، أو بوقت معيَّن أو بالدوام، أو بحين وصف الموضوع.
Chapter on propositions and their judgments.
- The special conditional [proposition] is similar to it, but with the exposition of negating perpetuity at the departure of the description: e.g., 'Every writer moves his fingers as long as he is writing, not perpetually.'
4. The temporal [proposition]: e.g., 'Every human necessarily moves his fingers at the time of writing.' It is called 'temporal' because it is restricted by time, and 'absolute' because it is not restricted by what follows.
5. The temporal non-described as absolute is similar to it, but with the exposition of negating perpetuity.
6. The absolute distributed [proposition] is like the temporal except that the time is unspecified: e.g., 'Every possible [thing] is non-existent necessarily at some time.'
- The non-described distributed [proposition] is similar to it, but with restriction. So these are the seven necessary [propositions]: the first is absolute, the two conditionals are restricted by the perpetuity of the description, the two temporals by a specific time, and the two distributed by an indefinite time. As for the perpetual [propositions]:
1. The absolute perpetual: e.g., 'Every sphere moves perpetually.'
2. The general customary [proposition]: 'What restricts its perpetuity by a description of the subject without exposition of negating perpetuity at the departure of that description': e.g., 'Every eater moves his lower jaw as long as he eats.' It is called 'customary' because in its perpetual relation it suffices with custom and habit, even if reason does not necessitate its perpetuity, as in the mentioned example, and 'general' because it is more general than that which follows. - The special customary [proposition] is similar to it with restriction. So if the word 'necessity' is removed from the examples of the first three necessary [propositions], they become examples for the three perpetual [propositions] in order.
So these are the three perpetual [propositions]: the first is absolute, and the two customaries are restricted by the perpetuity of the description.
As for the absolute [propositions]:
1. The general absolute: e.g., 'Every human dies with the general absolute.'
2. The existential non-necessary absolute: which is the one judged with the actuality of the relation with restriction by negating necessity: e.g., 'Every human dies not necessarily.' It is called 'existential' because its relation exists in act, and 'non-necessary' because it is restricted by negating necessity.
3. The existential non-perpetual is similar to it with restriction by negating perpetuity: e.g., 'Every human lives not perpetually.'
4. The temporal absolute [proposition] is: which restricts its actual relation to the time of the subject's description: e.g., 'Every writer moves his fingers absolutely when he is writing.'
And the difference between restriction by the time of the subject's description and restriction by its perpetual description: that restriction by the time of description does not encompass all its times, unlike perpetual description which encompasses all times of the subject's description. By this you know the difference between the general customary and the temporal absolute in terms of the restriction.
So these are the four absolute [propositions]: the first of them is absolute, and the three after it are restricted by negating perpetuity, by negating necessity, and by the time of the subject's description. As for the possible [propositions]:
1. The general possible: e.g., 'Every human is an animal with the general possibility'; because what is meant by it is what its relation is not impossible.
2. The special possible: what is judged in it that its relation is not impossible nor necessary, but permissible with equal sides: e.g., 'Every body moves with the special possibility.' It is called 'possible' because its modality is possibility, and 'special' because it is specific to the equal sides, so it is not verified by necessity, unlike the general.
3. The temporal possible is: which restricts its possibility to a specific time: e.g., 'Every human dies with the general possibility at the time of the soul's departure from him.' It is called 'possible' for what preceded, and 'temporal' because it restricts its modality of possibility to a specific time.
4. The conditional possible is: which restricts its possibility to the time of the subject's description: e.g., 'Every eater is hungry with possibility when he is eating.'
5. The perpetual possible: 'Which judges the perpetuity of possibility': e.g., 'Every possible [thing] is non-existent with possibility perpetually.'
So these are the five possible [propositions]: the first of them is absolute, and the four after it are restricted: either by specificity of possibility, or by a specific time, or by perpetuity, or by the time of the subject's description.
Source pages p. 603

Commentary
This passage is a detailed classification of modal propositions (qadaya) from the chapter on propositions. The author systematically enumerates the types of propositions based on their modality: necessity (ḍarūrī), perpetuity (dā’im), absolute (muṭlaq), and possibility (mumkin). Each category is subdivided with precise definitions and examples from everyday life (like writing, eating, movement). The classification follows the standard structure in Islamic logic, where the modality is determined by the quality (affirmative/negative) and the temporal or necessity conditions. The commentary then explains each subcategory: for necessary propositions, there are seven types including absolute, conditional, temporal, and distributed. For perpetual propositions, three types: absolute, general customary, and special customary. For absolute propositions, four types: general absolute, existential non-necessary, existential non-perpetual, and temporal absolute. For possible propositions, five types: general possible, special possible, temporal possible, conditional possible, and perpetual possible. The author also highlights the difference between restriction by the time of a description (which does not cover all times) and restriction by perpetual description (which covers all times), and contrasts the general customary with the temporal absolute. The examples are drawn from observable phenomena, such as 'every sphere moves perpetually' (a standard example in Aristotelian cosmology) and 'every human dies' (an absolute truth). This classification is foundational for understanding how propositions are used in syllogisms and in scientific demonstration.

قضية مشروطة عامة
قضية مشروطة خاصة
قضية وقتية
قضية منتشرة

The Three Perpetual Propositions
Author enumerates and defines the three perpetual propositions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three types of perpetual propositions (dāʾima) and explain how they differ from necessary propositions.

Core Idea
Perpetual propositions assert lasting truth without necessity, relying on custom or absolute continuity.

After necessary propositions, the author turns to perpetual propositions (dāʾima). These affirm that a judgment holds perpetually, but without the force of necessity. The three types are: absolute perpetual, general customary, and special customary. Understanding them is essential for distinguishing between what is always true by nature and what is habitually true.

Guided Path
1
Locate the perpetual propositions section
In the source, after the seven necessary propositions, the author begins 'Wa amma al-dawāʾim' (وأما الدوائم). Identify the three types listed.
2
Extract the restriction for each perpetual type
The absolute perpetual has no restriction beyond perpetuity. The general customary is restricted by the subject's description without negating perpetuity at departure. The special customary adds a negation.
3
Note the examples provided
The absolute perpetual example is 'Every sphere moves perpetually.' The general customary example is 'Every eater moves his lower jaw as long as he eats.' The special customary would be similar with an added negation.
4
Understand the relationship to necessary propositions
The author notes that removing the word 'necessity' from the first three necessary examples yields the three perpetual examples. This shows the close link but also the key difference: necessity vs. habit/custom.

- والمنتشرة غير الموصوفة بإطلاق مثلها، لكن مع التقييد، فهذه الضروريات السبع؛ الأولى مطلقة والمشروطتان مقيَّدتان بدوام الوصف والوقتيَّتان بوقت معيَّن، والمنتشرتان بوقت مبهم . وأما الدوائم :
۱ - فالدائمة المطلقة ؛ نحو: «كل فلك متحرك دائماً».
٢ - والعرفية العامة : «ما قيد دوامها بوصف الموضوع من غير تعرض لنفي الدوام عند مفارقة ذلك الوصف»؛ نحو: كلُّ آكل متحرك الفكِّ الأسفل ما دام أكلاً»، سميت: «عرفيَّة؛ للاكتفاء في دوام نسبتها بالعرف والعادة، وإن لم يقتض العقل دوامها، كما في المثال المذكور، وعامَّةٌ ; لأَنَّها أَعمُّ مِنَ الَّتي بعدها . - والعرفيَّةُ الخاصة مثلها مع التّقييد ; فأمثلةُ الضَّروريّات الثَّلاث الأُوَل إن حذف منها لفظ الضرورة ، صارت أمثلة للدوائم الثلاث على الترتيب.
فهذه الدَّوائم الثَّلاث : الأولى ،مطلقة، والعرفيَّتان مقيَّدتان بدوام الوصف.
وأما المطلقات :
۱ - فالمطلقة العامة ؛ نحو: كلُّ إنسان ميت بالإطلاق العام».
۲ - والمطلقة الوجوديَّة اللا ضروريَّة وهي : المحكوم فيها بفعليَّة النسبة مع التقييد بنفي الضرورة ; نحو: كلُّ إنسان فهو ميت لا بالضَّرورة»، سمّيت : «وجوديَّة؛ لوجود نسبتها بالفعل، و: «لا ضروريَّة; لتقييدها بنفي الضرورة.
٣ - والوجودية اللا دائمة مثلها مع التقييد بنفي التقييد بنفي الدوام ; نحو: «كل إنسان حي لا دائماً». ٤ - والمطلقة الحينيَّة هي : التي قيَّدت نسبتها الفعليَّة بحين وصف الموضوع»; نحو: كلُّ كاتب متحرك الأصابع بالإطلاق حين هو كاتب.
والفرقُ بين التَّقييد بحين وصف الموضوع والتَّقييد بدوام وصفه : أنَّ التَّقييد بحين الوصف لا يستغرق جميع أحيانه، بخلاف دوام الوصف يستغرق جميع أحيان وصف الموضوع، وبهذا تعرف الفرق بين العرفيّة العامة وبين المطلقة الحينيَّة من حيث القيد.
فهذه المطلقات الأربع الأولى منهنَّ مطلقة، والثَّلاث بعدها مقيدات بنفي الدوام، ونفي الضّرورة، وبحين وصف الموضوع. وأما الممكنات :
۱ - فالممكنة العامة; نحو: كلُّ إنسانٍ حَيَوَان بالإمكان العام ; لأنَّ المراد بها ما نسبتها غير ممتنعة .
٢ - والممكنة الخاصة : ما حكم فيها بأنَّ نسبتها غير ممتنعة ولا ضرورية، بل جائزة مستوية الطَّرفين»; نحو: كلُّ جرم متحرك بالإمكان الخاص»، سمّيت : «ممكنة»; لأنَّ جهتها إمكان، و «خاصَّةٌ» ; لاختصاصها بمستوي الطرفين، فلا تصدق بالضَّرورة، بخلاف العامة.
٣ - والممكنة الوقتيّة هي: التي قيَّد إمكانها بوقت معيَّن»; نحو: كلُّ إنسان ميت بالإمكان العام وقت مفارقة الرُّوح له سمّيت ممكنةً» لما سبق، ووقتيَّةٌ»; لتقييد جهة إمكانها بوقت معيَّن . ٤ - والممكنة الحينيَّة وهي : التي قيَّد إمكانها بحين وصف الموضوع»; نحو: «كل آكل جائع بالإمكان حين هو آكل».
ه - والممكنة الدائمة: «الَّتي حكم فيها بدوام الإمكان»; نحو: كلُّ ممكن معدوم بالإمكان دائماً .
فهذه الممكنات الخمس ; الأولى منهنَّ مطلقة، والأربع بعدها مقيَّدة; إما بخصوص الإمكان، أو بوقت معيَّن أو بالدوام، أو بحين وصف الموضوع.
Chapter on propositions and their judgments.
- The special conditional [proposition] is similar to it, but with the exposition of negating perpetuity at the departure of the description: e.g., 'Every writer moves his fingers as long as he is writing, not perpetually.'
4. The temporal [proposition]: e.g., 'Every human necessarily moves his fingers at the time of writing.' It is called 'temporal' because it is restricted by time, and 'absolute' because it is not restricted by what follows.
5. The temporal non-described as absolute is similar to it, but with the exposition of negating perpetuity.
6. The absolute distributed [proposition] is like the temporal except that the time is unspecified: e.g., 'Every possible [thing] is non-existent necessarily at some time.'
- The non-described distributed [proposition] is similar to it, but with restriction. So these are the seven necessary [propositions]: the first is absolute, the two conditionals are restricted by the perpetuity of the description, the two temporals by a specific time, and the two distributed by an indefinite time. As for the perpetual [propositions]:
1. The absolute perpetual: e.g., 'Every sphere moves perpetually.'
2. The general customary [proposition]: 'What restricts its perpetuity by a description of the subject without exposition of negating perpetuity at the departure of that description': e.g., 'Every eater moves his lower jaw as long as he eats.' It is called 'customary' because in its perpetual relation it suffices with custom and habit, even if reason does not necessitate its perpetuity, as in the mentioned example, and 'general' because it is more general than that which follows. - The special customary [proposition] is similar to it with restriction. So if the word 'necessity' is removed from the examples of the first three necessary [propositions], they become examples for the three perpetual [propositions] in order.
So these are the three perpetual [propositions]: the first is absolute, and the two customaries are restricted by the perpetuity of the description.
As for the absolute [propositions]:
1. The general absolute: e.g., 'Every human dies with the general absolute.'
2. The existential non-necessary absolute: which is the one judged with the actuality of the relation with restriction by negating necessity: e.g., 'Every human dies not necessarily.' It is called 'existential' because its relation exists in act, and 'non-necessary' because it is restricted by negating necessity.
3. The existential non-perpetual is similar to it with restriction by negating perpetuity: e.g., 'Every human lives not perpetually.'
4. The temporal absolute [proposition] is: which restricts its actual relation to the time of the subject's description: e.g., 'Every writer moves his fingers absolutely when he is writing.'
And the difference between restriction by the time of the subject's description and restriction by its perpetual description: that restriction by the time of description does not encompass all its times, unlike perpetual description which encompasses all times of the subject's description. By this you know the difference between the general customary and the temporal absolute in terms of the restriction.
So these are the four absolute [propositions]: the first of them is absolute, and the three after it are restricted by negating perpetuity, by negating necessity, and by the time of the subject's description. As for the possible [propositions]:
1. The general possible: e.g., 'Every human is an animal with the general possibility'; because what is meant by it is what its relation is not impossible.
2. The special possible: what is judged in it that its relation is not impossible nor necessary, but permissible with equal sides: e.g., 'Every body moves with the special possibility.' It is called 'possible' because its modality is possibility, and 'special' because it is specific to the equal sides, so it is not verified by necessity, unlike the general.
3. The temporal possible is: which restricts its possibility to a specific time: e.g., 'Every human dies with the general possibility at the time of the soul's departure from him.' It is called 'possible' for what preceded, and 'temporal' because it restricts its modality of possibility to a specific time.
4. The conditional possible is: which restricts its possibility to the time of the subject's description: e.g., 'Every eater is hungry with possibility when he is eating.'
5. The perpetual possible: 'Which judges the perpetuity of possibility': e.g., 'Every possible [thing] is non-existent with possibility perpetually.'
So these are the five possible [propositions]: the first of them is absolute, and the four after it are restricted: either by specificity of possibility, or by a specific time, or by perpetuity, or by the time of the subject's description.
Source pages p. 603

Commentary
This passage is a detailed classification of modal propositions (qadaya) from the chapter on propositions. The author systematically enumerates the types of propositions based on their modality: necessity (ḍarūrī), perpetuity (dā’im), absolute (muṭlaq), and possibility (mumkin). Each category is subdivided with precise definitions and examples from everyday life (like writing, eating, movement). The classification follows the standard structure in Islamic logic, where the modality is determined by the quality (affirmative/negative) and the temporal or necessity conditions. The commentary then explains each subcategory: for necessary propositions, there are seven types including absolute, conditional, temporal, and distributed. For perpetual propositions, three types: absolute, general customary, and special customary. For absolute propositions, four types: general absolute, existential non-necessary, existential non-perpetual, and temporal absolute. For possible propositions, five types: general possible, special possible, temporal possible, conditional possible, and perpetual possible. The author also highlights the difference between restriction by the time of a description (which does not cover all times) and restriction by perpetual description (which covers all times), and contrasts the general customary with the temporal absolute. The examples are drawn from observable phenomena, such as 'every sphere moves perpetually' (a standard example in Aristotelian cosmology) and 'every human dies' (an absolute truth). This classification is foundational for understanding how propositions are used in syllogisms and in scientific demonstration.

قضية دائمة
قضية دائمة مطلقة
قضية عرفية عامة
قضية عرفية خاصة

Checkpoint
What is the example given for the general customary perpetual proposition?
A) Every sphere moves perpetually.
B) Every writer moves his fingers as long as he writes.
C) Every human dies absolutely.
D) Every eater moves his lower jaw as long as he eats.

Key Takeaway
Perpetual propositions express lasting truths grounded in custom or physical continuity, not in absolute necessity.

The Four Absolute Propositions
Author enumerates and defines the four absolute propositions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to differentiate among the four absolute propositions (muṭlaqa) based on their restrictions: existential non-necessary, existential non-perpetual, and temporal absolute.

Core Idea
Absolute propositions assert actuality without necessity, with three subtypes specifying negations of necessity, perpetuity, or time restrictions.

The third category in the classification is absolute propositions (muṭlaqa). These affirm a judgment as actual (bi-al-fi‘l) but without the claim of necessity. The source lists four types: the general absolute, existential non-necessary, existential non-perpetual, and temporal absolute. This lesson clarifies each subtype and the crucial difference between temporal restriction and perpetual restriction.

Guided Path
1
Locate the absolute propositions section
In the source, after the perpetual section, the author begins 'Wa amma al-muṭlaqāt' (وأما المطلقات). Identify the four types listed.
2
Extract the defining feature for each absolute type
The general absolute is unrestricted. The existential non-necessary negates necessity. The existential non-perpetual negates perpetuity. The temporal absolute restricts to the time of the subject's description.
3
Note the examples provided
Examples: 'Every human dies' (general absolute), 'Every human dies not necessarily' (existential non-necessary), 'Every human lives not perpetually' (existential non-perpetual), 'Every writer moves his fingers absolutely when he is writing' (temporal absolute).
4
Understand the difference between temporal absolute and general customary perpetual
The source explicitly differentiates them: temporal absolute restricts to a specific time (ḥīn) while general customary perpetual covers all times of the description. This is a key analytical point.

باب في القضايا وأحكامها
- والمشروطة الخاصة مثلها، لكن مع التَّعرُّض لنفي الدوام عند مفارقة الوصف؛ نحو: كلُّ كاتب متحرك الأصابع ما دام كاتباً لا دائماً».
٤ - والوقتيَّة ؛ نحو: كلُّ إنسان متحرّك الأصابع بالضَّرورة وقت الكتابة»، سميت : «وقتيَّةٌ لتقييدها بالوقت، ومطلقة؛ لعدم تقييدها بما يأتي.
٥ - والوقتية غير الموصوفة بإطلاق مثلها، لكن مع التعرض لنفي الدوام.

Chapter on propositions and their judgments.
- The special conditional [proposition] is similar to it, but with the exposition of negating perpetuity at the departure of the description: e.g., 'Every writer moves his fingers as long as he is writing, not perpetually.'
4. The temporal [proposition]: e.g., 'Every human necessarily moves his fingers at the time of writing.' It is called 'temporal' because it is restricted by time, and 'absolute' because it is not restricted by what follows.

As for the perpetual [propositions]:
1. The absolute perpetual: e.g., 'Every sphere moves perpetually.'

1. The general possible: e.g., 'Every human is an animal with the general possibility'; because what is meant by it is what its relation is not impossible.

Commentary
This passage is a detailed classification of modal propositions (qadaya) from the chapter on propositions. The author systematically enumerates the types of propositions based on their modality: necessity (ḍarūrī), perpetuity (dā’im), absolute (muṭlaq), and possibility (mumkin). Each category is subdivided with precise definitions and examples from everyday life (like writing, eating, movement). The classification follows the standard structure in Islamic logic, where the modality is determined by the quality (affirmative/negative) and the temporal or necessity conditions. For possible propositions, five types: general possible, special possible, temporal possible, conditional possible, and perpetual possible. The examples are drawn from observable phenomena, such as 'every sphere moves perpetually' (a standard example in Aristotelian cosmology) and 'every human dies' (an absolute truth). The Five Possible Propositions
Author enumerates and defines the five possible propositions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify the five possible propositions (mumkina) and explain the difference between general possibility and special possibility.

Core Idea
Possible propositions cover what is neither necessary nor impossible, with five subtypes varying by generality, time, description, and duration.

The final category in the classification is possible propositions (mumkina). These assert that a judgment is not impossible and not necessary. The source enumerates five types: general possible, special possible, temporal possible, conditional possible, and perpetual possible. This lesson unpacks each type, emphasizing the critical distinction between general and special possibility.

Guided Path
1
Locate the possible propositions section
In the source, after the absolute section, the author begins 'Wa amma al-mumkināt' (وأما الممكنات). Identify the five types listed.
2
Extract the defining feature for each possible type
The general possible only denies impossibility. The special possible denies both necessity and impossibility (equal possibility). The temporal possible restricts possibility to a specific time. The conditional possible restricts to the time of the subject's description. The perpetual possible asserts possibility perpetually.
3
Note the examples provided
Examples: 'Every human is an animal' (general possible), 'Every body moves' (special possible), 'Every human dies at the time of death' (temporal possible), 'Every eater is hungry when he eats' (conditional possible), 'Every possible is non-existent perpetually' (perpetual possible).
4
Understand the difference between general and special possible
General possible includes necessary truths (since they are not impossible), while special possible excludes necessity. The source notes that special possible is 'specific to equal sides' and does not apply to necessary judgments.

٥ - والوقتية غير الموصوفة بإطلاق مثلها، لكن مع التعرض لنفي الدوام.

والفرقُ بين التَّقييد بحين وصف الموضوع والتَّقييد بدوام وصفه : أنَّ التَّقييد بحين الوصف لا يستغرق جميع أحيانه، بخلاف دوام الوصف يستغرق جميع أحيان وصف الموضوع، وبهذا تعرف الفرق بين العرفيّة العامة وبين المطلقة الحينيَّة من حيث القيد.
فهذه المطلقات الأربع الأولى منهنَّ مطلقة، والثَّلاث بعدها مقيدات بنفي الدوام، ونفي الضّرورة، وبحين وصف الموضوع. وأما الممكنات :
۱ - فالممكنة العامة; نحو: كلُّ إنسانٍ حَيَوَان بالإمكان العام ; لأنَّ المراد بها ما نسبتها غير ممتنعة .
٢ - والممكنة الخاصة : ما حكم فيها بأنَّ نسبتها غير ممتنعة ولا ضرورية، بل جائزة مستوية الطَّرفين»; نحو: كلُّ جرم متحرك بالإمكان الخاص»، سمّيت : «ممكنة»; لأنَّ جهتها إمكان، و «خاصَّةٌ» ; لاختصاصها بمستوي الطرفين، فلا تصدق بالضَّرورة، بخلاف العامة.
٣ - والممكنة الوقتيّة هي: التي قيَّد إمكانها بوقت معيَّن»; نحو: كلُّ إنسان ميت بالإمكان العام وقت مفارقة الرُّوح له سمّيت ممكنةً» لما سبق، ووقتيَّةٌ»; لتقييد جهة إمكانها بوقت معيَّن . ٤ - والممكنة الحينيَّة وهي : التي قيَّد إمكانها بحين وصف الموضوع»; نحو: «كل آكل جائع بالإمكان حين هو آكل».

فهذه الممكنات الخمس ; الأولى منهنَّ مطلقة، والأربع بعدها مقيَّدة; إما بخصوص الإمكان، أو بوقت معيَّن أو بالدوام، أو بحين وصف الموضوع.
Chapter on propositions and their judgments.
- The special conditional [proposition] is similar to it, but with the exposition of negating perpetuity at the departure of the description: e.g., 'Every writer moves his fingers as long as he is writing, not perpetually.'
4. The temporal [proposition]: e.g., 'Every human necessarily moves his fingers at the time of writing.' It is called 'temporal' because it is restricted by time, and 'absolute' because it is not restricted by what follows.
5. The temporal non-described as absolute is similar to it, but with the exposition of negating perpetuity.
6. The absolute distributed [proposition] is like the temporal except that the time is unspecified: e.g., 'Every possible [thing] is non-existent necessarily at some time.'
- The non-described distributed [proposition] is similar to it, but with restriction. So these are the seven necessary [propositions]: the first is absolute, the two conditionals are restricted by the perpetuity of the description, the two temporals by a specific time, and the two distributed by an indefinite time. As for the perpetual [propositions]:
1. The absolute perpetual: e.g., 'Every sphere moves perpetually.'
2. The general customary [proposition]: 'What restricts its perpetuity by a description of the subject without exposition of negating perpetuity at the departure of that description': e.g., 'Every eater moves his lower jaw as long as he eats.' It is called 'customary' because in its perpetual relation it suffices with custom and habit, even if reason does not necessitate its perpetuity, as in the mentioned example, and 'general' because it is more general than that which follows. - The special customary [proposition] is similar to it with restriction. So if the word 'necessity' is removed from the examples of the first three necessary [propositions], they become examples for the three perpetual [propositions] in order.
So these are the three perpetual [propositions]: the first is absolute, and the two customaries are restricted by the perpetuity of the description.
As for the absolute [propositions]:
1. The general absolute: e.g., 'Every human dies with the general absolute.'
2. The existential non-necessary absolute: which is the one judged with the actuality of the relation with restriction by negating necessity: e.g., 'Every human dies not necessarily.' It is called 'existential' because its relation exists in act, and 'non-necessary' because it is restricted by negating necessity.
3. The existential non-perpetual is similar to it with restriction by negating perpetuity: e.g., 'Every human lives not perpetually.'
4. The temporal absolute [proposition] is: which restricts its actual relation to the time of the subject's description: e.g., 'Every writer moves his fingers absolutely when he is writing.'
And the difference between restriction by the time of the subject's description and restriction by its perpetual description: that restriction by the time of description does not encompass all its times, unlike perpetual description which encompasses all times of the subject's description. By this you know the difference between the general customary and the temporal absolute in terms of the restriction.
So these are the four absolute [propositions]: the first of them is absolute, and the three after it are restricted by negating perpetuity, by negating necessity, and by the time of the subject's description. As for the possible [propositions]:
1. The general possible: e.g., 'Every human is an animal with the general possibility'; because what is meant by it is what its relation is not impossible.
2. The special possible: what is judged in it that its relation is not impossible nor necessary, but permissible with equal sides: e.g., 'Every body moves with the special possibility.' It is called 'possible' because its modality is possibility, and 'special' because it is specific to the equal sides, so it is not verified by necessity, unlike the general.
3. The temporal possible is: which restricts its possibility to a specific time: e.g., 'Every human dies with the general possibility at the time of the soul's departure from him.' It is called 'possible' for what preceded, and 'temporal' because it restricts its modality of possibility to a specific time.
4. The conditional possible is: which restricts its possibility to the time of the subject's description: e.g., 'Every eater is hungry with possibility when he is eating.'
5. The perpetual possible: 'Which judges the perpetuity of possibility': e.g., 'Every possible [thing] is non-existent with possibility perpetually.'
So these are the five possible [propositions]: the first of them is absolute, and the four after it are restricted: either by specificity of possibility, or by a specific time, or by perpetuity, or by the time of the subject's description.
Source pages p. 603

Commentary
This passage is a detailed classification of modal propositions (qadaya) from the chapter on propositions. The author systematically enumerates the types of propositions based on their modality: necessity (ḍarūrī), perpetuity (dā’im), absolute (muṭlaq), and possibility (mumkin). Each category is subdivided with precise definitions and examples from everyday life (like writing, eating, movement). The classification follows the standard structure in Islamic logic, where the modality is determined by the quality (affirmative/negative) and the temporal or necessity conditions. The commentary then explains each subcategory: for necessary propositions, there are seven types including absolute, conditional, temporal, and distributed. For perpetual propositions, three types: absolute, general customary, and special customary. For absolute propositions, four types: general absolute, existential non-necessary, existential non-perpetual, and temporal absolute. For possible propositions, five types: general possible, special possible, temporal possible, conditional possible, and perpetual possible. The author also highlights the difference between restriction by the time of a description (which does not cover all times) and restriction by perpetual description (which covers all times), and contrasts the general customary with the temporal absolute. The examples are drawn from observable phenomena, such as 'every sphere moves perpetually' (a standard example in Aristotelian cosmology) and 'every human dies' (an absolute truth). This classification is foundational for understanding how propositions are used in syllogisms and in scientific demonstration.

قضية ممكنة خاصة
قضية ممكنة وقتية
قضية ممكنة حينية
قضية ممكنة دائمة
