The Four Types of Opposition (Taqābul)
Author classifies the four types of logical opposition: contradiction, contrariety, privation/possession, and correlation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the four types of opposition and define each using the general definition of mutual opposites.

Core Idea
Four types of opposition: only contradiction has no middle.

Logicians classify opposition into four distinct types: contrariety, correlation, privation/possession, and contradiction. Each type has a unique logical behavior. This lesson will help you identify them and understand their defining characteristics.

Guided Path
1
List the four types
From the passage, identify the four types: taḍādd (contrariety), taḍāyuf (correlation), 'adam wa malaka (privation/possession), tanāquḍ (contradiction).
2
Define mutual opposites
The general definition: two things that cannot coexist in one subject at one time from one aspect.
This definition applies to all four types.
3
Focus on contraries and contradictories
The passage gives specific definitions for these two: contraries can both be absent, contradictories cannot.
Note the key difference: presence of a middle state.
4
Test with an example
Consider 'hot' and 'cold': they are contraries because something can be lukewarm. 'Hot' and 'not hot' are contradictories.
Use Islamic examples like 'wajib' and 'haram' (contraries if third option possible).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبيه: أَنْوَاعُ التَّقَابُلِ أَرْبَعَةٌ : تَقَابُلُ التَّضَادُ، وَتَقَابُلُ التَّضَايُفِ ، وَتَقَابُلُ العَدَمِ وَالمَلَكَةِ، وَتَقَابُلُ التَّنَاقُضِ. وَقَدْ عَرَّفَ الحُكَمَاءُ «المُتَقَابِلَيْنِ»: بِأَنَّهُمَا أَمْرَانِ لَا يَجْتَمِعَانِ فِي زَمَنٍ وَاحِدٍ فِي ذَاتٍ وَاحِدَةٍ مِنْ جِهَةٍ وَاحِدَةٍ»، كَمَا عَرَّفُوا «المِثْلَيْنِ»: «بِكُلِّ اثْنَيْنِ اشْتَرَكَا فِي تَمَامِ المَاهِيَةِ». قَالَ: «الضِّدَّانِ : هُمَا اللَّذَانِ لَا يَجْتَمِعَانِ وَيُمْكِنُ ارْتِفَاعُهُمَا كَالسَّوَادِ وَالبَيَاضِ ; إِذْ يُمْكِنُ ارْتِفَاعُهُمَا بِالحُمْرَةِ وَالخُضْرَةِ. وَالنَّقِيضَانِ: هُمَا اللَّذَانِ لَا يَجْتَمِعَانِ وَلَا يَرْتَفِعَانِ».
A notice: The types of opposition are four: opposition of contrariety, opposition of correlation, opposition of privation and possession, and opposition of contradiction. And the philosophers have defined 'the two mutual opposites' as: 'two things that do not come together in one time in one essence from one aspect', just as they defined 'the two similars' as: 'every two that share in the complete quiddity'. He said: 'The two contraries: they are two that do not come together and it is possible for both to be eliminated, like black and white; for it is possible for both to be eliminated by redness and greenness. And the two contradictories: they are two that do not come together and cannot both be eliminated.'
Source pages p. 642

Commentary
This passage introduces the classification of opposition (taqābul) into four types. It begins with a 'notice' (tanbīh) that the types are four: (1) taḍādd (contrariety), (2) taḍāyuf (correlation), (3) 'adam wa al-malaka (privation and possession), and (4) tanāquḍ (contradiction). The author then quotes the philosophers' definition of 'mutual opposites' (al-mutaqābilān) as two things that cannot coexist in one subject at one time from one aspect. This is a general definition covering all four types. In contrast, 'similars' (al-mithlān) are two things that share the same complete quiddity (e.g., two instances of the same species). The passage then specifies two subtypes within opposition: the two contraries (al-ḍiddān) like black and white—they cannot coexist, but it is possible for both to be absent (e.g., a red object has neither black nor white). The two contradictories (al-naqīḍān) like existence and non-existence—they cannot coexist and cannot both be absent; one must be true. This distinguishes contradiction from contrariety: in contradiction, there is no middle state; in contrariety, a middle state is possible.

Key Terms
التقابل (al-taqābul): هو علاقة بين أمرين لا يجتمعان في زمن واحد في ذات واحدة من جهة واحدة [Note: This is the standard definition; stable across the tradition.]
التضاد (al-taḍādd): تقابل بين أمرين لا يجتمعان ويمكن ارتفاعهما، كالسواد والبياض [Note: Stable; defined here as a type of opposition with possible middle.]
التناقض (al-tanāquḍ): تقابل بين أمرين لا يجتمعان ولا يرتفعان، كالوجود والعدم [Note: Stable; distinguished from taḍādd by impossibility of both being false.]
المتقابلان (al-mutaqābilān): هما أمران لا يجتمعان في زمن واحد في ذات واحدة من جهة واحدة [Note: General term covering all four types.]
المثلان (al-mithlān): كل اثنين اشتركا في تمام الماهية (مثل فردين من نوع واحد) [Note: Stable; used to contrast with opposites.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Contrariety (taḍādd)
B) Correlation (taḍāyuf)
C) Privation/possession ('adam wa malaka)
D) Contradiction (tanāquḍ)

Key Takeaway
Opposition is classified into four types, with the critical distinction being whether both can be false (contrariety, correlation, privation/possession) or not (contradiction).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Contrariety vs. Contradiction: The Middle Ground
Author classifies the four types of logical opposition: contradiction, contrariety, privation/possession, and correlation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between contrariety and contradiction by applying the test of whether a middle state is possible.

Core Idea
Contraries can both be false; contradictories cannot.

Among the four types of opposition, two are most frequently encountered in arguments: contrariety and contradiction. The key difference lies in whether a middle state exists. This lesson sharpens your ability to tell them apart.

Guided Path
1
Recall the definitions
From the passage: contraries cannot coexist but can both be absent; contradictories cannot coexist nor can both be absent.
Write the Arabic definitions: الضدان لا يجتمعان ويمكن ارتفاعهما، النقيضان لا يجتمعان ولا يرتفعان.
2
Test for a middle state
For any pair of opposites, ask: Can a third thing be true that makes both false? If yes, they are contraries; if no, they are contradictories.
Example: 'black' and 'white' – a red object is neither, so contraries.
3
Apply to Islamic legal rulings
Consider 'wajib' and 'haram': an act can be mubah, so these are contraries. 'Wajib' and 'not wajib' are contradictories.
Use terms from fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبيه: أَنْوَاعُ التَّقَابُلِ أَرْبَعَةٌ : تَقَابُلُ التَّضَادُ، وَتَقَابُلُ التَّضَايُفِ ، وَتَقَابُلُ العَدَمِ وَالمَلَكَةِ، وَتَقَابُلُ التَّنَاقُضِ. وَقَدْ عَرَّفَ الحُكَمَاءُ «المُتَقَابِلَيْنِ»: بِأَنَّهُمَا أَمْرَانِ لَا يَجْتَمِعَانِ فِي زَمَنٍ وَاحِدٍ فِي ذَاتٍ وَاحِدَةٍ مِنْ جِهَةٍ وَاحِدَةٍ»، كَمَا عَرَّفُوا «المِثْلَيْنِ»: «بِكُلِّ اثْنَيْنِ اشْتَرَكَا فِي تَمَامِ المَاهِيَةِ». قَالَ: «الضِّدَّانِ : هُمَا اللَّذَانِ لَا يَجْتَمِعَانِ وَيُمْكِنُ ارْتِفَاعُهُمَا كَالسَّوَادِ وَالبَيَاضِ ; إِذْ يُمْكِنُ ارْتِفَاعُهُمَا بِالحُمْرَةِ وَالخُضْرَةِ. وَالنَّقِيضَانِ: هُمَا اللَّذَانِ لَا يَجْتَمِعَانِ وَلَا يَرْتَفِعَانِ».
A notice: The types of opposition are four: opposition of contrariety, opposition of correlation, opposition of privation and possession, and opposition of contradiction. And the philosophers have defined 'the two mutual opposites' as: 'two things that do not come together in one time in one essence from one aspect', just as they defined 'the two similars' as: 'every two that share in the complete quiddity'. He said: 'The two contraries: they are two that do not come together and it is possible for both to be eliminated, like black and white; for it is possible for both to be eliminated by redness and greenness. And the two contradictories: they are two that do not come together and cannot both be eliminated.'

Commentary
This passage introduces the classification of opposition (taqābul) into four types. It begins with a 'notice' (tanbīh) that the types are four: (1) taḍādd (contrariety), (2) taḍāyuf (correlation), (3) 'adam wa al-malaka (privation and possession), and (4) tanāquḍ (contradiction). The author then quotes the philosophers' definition of 'mutual opposites' (al-mutaqābilān) as two things that cannot coexist in one subject at one time from one aspect. This is a general definition covering all four types. In contrast, 'similars' (al-mithlān) are two things that share the same complete quiddity (e.g., two instances of the same species). The passage then specifies two subtypes within opposition: the two contraries (al-ḍiddān) like black and white—they cannot coexist, but it is possible for both to be absent (e.g., a red object has neither black nor white). The two contradictories (al-naqīḍān) like existence and non-existence—they cannot coexist and cannot both be absent; one must be true. This distinguishes contradiction from contrariety: in contradiction, there is no middle state; in contrariety, a middle state is possible.

Key Terms
التضاد (al-taḍādd): تقابل بين أمرين لا يجتمعان ويمكن ارتفاعهما، كالسواد والبياض [Note: Stable; defined here as a type of opposition with possible middle.]
التناقض (al-tanāquḍ): تقابل بين أمرين لا يجتمعان ولا يرتفعان، كالوجود والعدم [Note: Stable; distinguished from taḍādd by impossibility of both being false.]
المتقابلان (al-mutaqābilān): هما أمران لا يجتمعان في زمن واحد في ذات واحدة من جهة واحدة [Note: General term covering all four types.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the possibility of both being eliminated (إمكان الارتفاع) characterize?
A) Mutual opposites (المتقابلان)
B) Contraries (الضدان)
C) Contradictories (النقيضان)
D) Similars (المثلان)

Key Takeaway
The crucial difference between contrariety and contradiction is whether a middle state is possible: contraries have a middle, contradictories do not.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
For each pair, determine if they are contraries or contradictories: (a) 'The Quran is created' vs. 'The Quran is uncreated'; (b) 'Zakat is obligatory' vs. 'Zakat is not obligatory'. Explain using the middle state test.
?
Construct a pair of contraries using terms from Islamic ethics (e.g., 'generous' and 'stingy' – middle is 'moderate').

The Four Types of Opposition (Taqabul)
Author enumerates and defines the four types of opposition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and distinguish all four types of opposition (taqabul) in logical texts using the criteria of coexistence and possibility of absence.

Core Idea
Opposition is defined by impossibility of coexistence; the four types differ by whether both can be absent.

In Islamic logic, understanding opposition (taqabul) is essential for analyzing propositions and arguments. The philosophers divided opposition into four types: contrariety, correlativity, privation-possession, and contradiction. This lesson breaks down each type using the key criteria from the passage: can they coexist? can both be absent?

Guided Path
1
Identify the type name
Locate one of the four Arabic terms: تضاد, تضايف, عدم وملكة, تناقض. Each represents a distinct type of opposition.
The passage lists them in order.
2
Check coexistence condition
For each pair, determine whether the two opposites can be present together in the same subject at the same time. All four types share that they cannot coexist.
Coexistence is impossible for all opposites by definition.
3
Check absence possibility
For contrariety, both can be absent (e.g., black and white can both be absent in gray). For contradiction, both cannot be absent (one must be true). For correlativity and privation-possession, the absence condition must be derived from their definitions.
This is the key distinguishing feature from the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أَنْوَاعُ التَّقَابُلِ أَرْبَعَةٌ : تَقَابُلُ التَّضَادُ، وَتَقَابُلُ التَّضَايُفِ ، وَتَقَابُلُ العَدَمِ وَالمَلَكَةِ، وَتَقَابُلُ التَّنَاقُضِ. قوله : (أَنْوَاعُ التَّقَابُلِ) قد عرَّف الحكماء المتقابلين»: بأنَّهما أمران لا يجتمعان في زمنٍ واحدٍ في ذاتٍ واحدة من جهةٍ واحدةٍ»، كما عرَّفوا المثلين»: «بكل اثنين اشتركا في تمام الماهية» قوله : (تَقَابُلُ التَّضَادُ الضّدَّان : هما اللذان لا يجتمعان ويمكن ارتفاعهما كالسواد والبياض ؛ إذ يمكن ارتفاعهما بالحمرة ،والخضرة والنَّقيضان: «هما اللذان لا يجتمعان ولا يرتفعان». ثم ذكر باقي الأنواع.
The types of opposition are four: opposition of contraries, opposition of correlatives, opposition of privation and possession, and opposition of contradiction. His statement: 'Types of opposition' – the philosophers have defined 'opposites' as 'two things that do not coexist in one time in one essence from one aspect,' just as they defined 'similarities' as 'every two that share in the complete essence.' His statement: 'Opposition of contraries' – the two contraries are those that do not coexist but both can be absent, like blackness and whiteness, for they can both be absent in redness and greenness. And the two contradictories: 'they are the two that do not coexist and do not both become absent.' Then he mentioned the remaining types.
Source pages p. 642

Commentary
This passage presents the standard division of opposition (taqābul) into four types, a foundational classification in logic. The author first lists them: (1) taḍād (contrariety), (2) taḍāyuf (correlativity), (3) 'adam wa-malaka (privation and possession), and (4) tanāquḍ (contradiction). He then provides the general definition of 'opposites' as understood by the philosophers (ḥukamā'): two things that cannot coexist in the same subject at the same time in the same respect. He contrasts this with 'similarities' (mathalān). Then he elaborates on the first type, contrariety, using the classic example of black and white: they cannot both be present simultaneously, but both can be absent (e.g., a green object is neither black nor white). In contrast, he mentions that contradictories (naqīḍān) cannot coexist and also cannot both be absent (since one must be true and the other false). The phrase 'then he mentioned the remaining types' indicates that the commentary will proceed to explain the other three types, but the passage stops here. This enumeration is a memorization anchor for students.

Key Terms
تقابل
تضاد
تضايف
عدم وملكة
تناقض

D) Contradiction (tanāquḍ)

Key Takeaway
Opposition has four types; the critical distinction is whether both opposites can be absent (contrariety, correlativity, privation-possession) or not (contradiction).

Division of Opposites into Existent and Non-Existent
Author classifies opposites based on whether they are existent or non-existent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any given pair of opposites into one of the four types (correlatives, contraries, privation/possession, contradiction) by applying the conditions from this passage.

Core Idea
Opposites are either both existent or one existent and one non-existent, with further sub‑divisions.

The author of the matn enumerates the types of opposition (taqābul) that are possible. This classification is essential for understanding how terms and propositions can be contradictory – a foundational tool in Islamic logic. Let us walk through each branch of the division and see what distinguishes one type from another.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main division
Read the first sentence: the two opposites are either both existent (wujūdiyān) or one existent and one non-existent ('adamī). Note that the author assumes two opposites cannot both be non-existent.
2
Distinguish correlatives from contraries
When both opposites are existent, ask: does the conceptualization of one depend on the other? If yes (e.g., father and son), they are correlatives (mutadāyifān). If no (e.g., white and black), they are contraries (didān).
In correlatives, each opposite is understood only in relation to the other.
3
Distinguish privation/possession from contradiction
When one opposite is existent and the other non-existent, check whether the non-existent term implies the absence of a quality from a subject that naturally receives it (e.g., blindness in a person). If yes, it is privation and possession ('adam wa-malaka). If no (e.g., blackness and its simple negation), it is contradiction (naqīḍān).
The subject's capacity is key: a wall cannot be called blind, so 'blindness' is not a privation for a wall.
4
Apply the classification to a new pair
Take a pair like 'knowledge' and 'ignorance' in a human being. Both are existent? No, ignorance is a privation of knowledge. The subject (human) is receptive to knowledge, so this falls under privation/possession.
This shows how the division works in a real Islamic science example (epistemology and kalām).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في التناقض وَوَجْهُ الحَصْرِ : أَنَّ المُتَقَابِلَيْنِ : إِمَّا وُجُودِيَّانِ ، أَوْ أَحَدُهُمَا وُجُودِيٌّ وَالآخَرُ عَدَمِيٌّ، فَالوُجُودِيَّانِ إِنْ تَوَقَّفَ تَعَقُلُ أَحَدِهِمَا عَلَى تَعَقُلِ الْآخَرِ كَـ : الأُبُوَّةِ، وَالبَنوَّةِ» فَالمُتَضَايفَانِ، أَوْ لَا كَـ : «البَيَاضِ ، وَالسَّوَادِ فَالضَّدَّانِ، وَاللَّذَانِ أَحَدُهُمَا وُجُودِيٌّ وَالآخَرُ عَدَمِيٌّ إِنِ اعْتُبِرَ في العَدَمِيِّ كَوْنُ المَحَلِّ قَابِلا لِلوُجُودِي كَـ : البَصَرِ، وَالعَمَى بِالنِّسْبَةِ إِلَى زَيْدٍ مَثَلاً، بِخِلَافِ الحَائِطِ فَعَدَمٌ وَمَلَكَةٌ ، وَإِنْ لَمْ يُعْتَبَرُ كَـ السَّوَادِ وَنَفْيهِ، فَالنَّقِيضَانِ، وَهَذَا مَبْنِي عَلَى أَنَّ المُتَقَابِلَيْنِ لَا يَكُونَانِ عَدَمَيْنِ .
A chapter on contradiction. And the basis of the enumeration: the two opposites are either both existent, or one existent and the other non-existent. If both existent: if the conceptualization of one depends on the conceptualization of the other, like fatherhood and sonship, then they are correlatives; if not, like whiteness and blackness, then they are contraries. And the two, one of which is existent and the other non-existent: if consideration is given in the non-existent to the subject being receptive to the existent, like sight and blindness with respect to Zaid, for instance, in contrast to a wall, then it is privation and possession; and if not considered, like blackness and its negation, then they are contradictories. And this is based on the premise that the two opposites cannot both be non-existent.
Source pages p. 643

Commentary
This passage is a logical division explaining why there are exactly four types of opposition. The author first divides opposites into those that are both existent (wujūdiyān) and those where one is existent and the other non-existent ('adamī). Among the existent pair, if they are mutually dependent in conception (one understood only in relation to the other), they are correlatives (e.g., father and son); if not, they are contraries (e.g., white and black). For the mixed pair (one existent, one non-existent), the division depends on whether the subject naturally possesses the quality in question: if the non-existent term implies the absence of a quality from a subject that normally would have it (like blindness in a person, but not in a wall), it is privation and possession; if no such consideration is made (like blackness and its simple negation 'not-black'), it is contradiction. The author notes that this classification assumes that two opposites cannot both be non-existent (i.e., contradictory terms are not both non-existent).

Key Terms
وجوديان
عدمي
متضايفان
ضدان
عدم وملكة
نقيضان

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Contrariety
C) Privation and possession
D) Contradiction

Key Takeaway
Opposites are divided into four types based on existence and the subject's receptivity, and this classification is fundamental for logical analysis in Islamic sciences.

Refining the Division of Opposites: When Both Sides are Non-Existent
Author addresses the possibility of opposition between two non-existents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify cases where two non-existents are contradictory opposites and correctly apply the refined division of oppositions.

Core Idea
Contradiction can exist between two negatives, not just a positive and a negative.

Al-Sa'd (al-Taftazani) critiques a common view that opposites must involve at least one positive existent. He points out that later scholars unanimously hold that the contradictory of a non-existent can itself be non-existent, as in 'impossibility' and 'non-impossibility'. In this lesson, we unpack his refinement and see how it corrects the standard enumeration of logical oppositions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim being refined
The earlier view implied that opposites cannot both be non-existent. Al-Sa'd rejects this, stating there is no proof for it and citing later scholars who affirm that the contradictory of a non-existent is non-existent.
This is a critical refinement of the division of opposites.
2
Find the examples given
Al-Sa'd gives examples: impossibility (imtina') and non-impossibility (la imtina'), blindness (ama) and non-blindness (la ama). Both pairs are opposites, and both sides are non-existent in the sense of privation or negation.
Blindness is a privation (lack of sight), non-blindness is the negation of that privation.
3
Understand why these are both non-existent
Blindness is a privation (non-existence of sight in a subject that should have it). Non-blindness is the absolute negation of blindness. Both are non-existential concepts, yet they are genuine contradictories.
This shows that contradictory opposition does not require a positive existent.
4
Examine the commentator's suggested refinement
The commentator proposes rewording the enumeration: first divide into existent or not. For non-existents, if it is negation from a receptive subject, it is privation-possession; otherwise, it is contradiction. This explicitly includes cases like blindness/non-blindness.
The refined wording avoids excluding valid non-existential opposites.
5
Test the refined division on a new case
Consider 'knowledge' (positive) and 'non-knowledge' (negation). Non-knowledge is the contradictory of knowledge. According to the refined division, since non-knowledge is not from a receptive subject (it is absolute negation), it falls under contradiction.
Contrast with 'sight' and 'blindness': blindness is from a receptive subject, so it is privation-possession.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ السَّعْدُ : وَلَيْسَ عَلَيْهِ دَلِيلٌ ، وَقَدْ أَطْبَقَ المُتَأخُرُونَ عَلَى أَنَّ نَقِيضُ العَدَمِي يَكُونُ عَدَمِيًّا كَـ : الامْتِنَاعِ وَاللَّا امْتِنَاعِ، وَالعَمَى وَاللَّا عَمَى. اهـ. وَهَذَا دَاخِلٌ فِي تَقَابُلِ التَّناقُضِ ؛ لِأَنَّ نَقِيضَ كُلِّ شَيْءٍ رَفْعُهُ؛ سَوَاءٌ كَانَ ذَلِكَ الشَّيْءُ ثُبُوتِيَّا أَوْ سَلْبِيًّا، فَلَوْ قِيلَ فِي وَجْهِ الحَصْرِ : الأَمْرَانِ إِمَّا وُجُودِيَّانِ أَوْ لَا، وَغَيْرُ الوُجُودِيَّيْنِ إِمَّا تَقَابُلُ أَمْرٍ وَسَلْبُهُ عَنْ مَحَلٌّ يَقْبَلُهُ، فَهُوَ تَقَابُلُ العَدَم وَالمَلَكَةِ، وَإِمَّا تَقَابُلُ أَمْرٍ وَسَلْبُه مُطلَقاً ، فَهُوَ تَقَابُلُ التَّناقُضِ لَشَمَلَ مَا ذَكَرَ، وَاللهُ تَعَالَى أَعْلَمُ .
Al-Sa'd said: There is no proof for it, and the later scholars have unanimously agreed that the contradictory of a non-existent is also non-existent, like impossibility and non-impossibility, and blindness and non-blindness. End. So this falls under the opposition of contradiction, because the contradictory of anything is its removal, whether that thing is positive or negative. If one were to say in the basis of the enumeration: the two matters are either both existent or not, and in the case of non-existent, either it is the opposition of a thing and its negation from a receptive subject, so it is privation and possession, or it is the opposition of a thing and its negation absolutely, so it is the opposition of contradictories, then it would include what was mentioned. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 643

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement by the commentator. He quotes al-Sa'd (al-Taftazani) who objects to the earlier claim that opposites cannot both be non-existent. Al-Sa'd asserts that there is no proof for that, and the later scholars agree that the contradictory of a non-existent is also non-existent, such as 'impossibility' and 'non-impossibility', or 'blindness' and 'non-blindness'. This shows that both contradictories can be non-existent (e.g., 'blindness' is a privation, 'non-blindness' is a negation of privation). The commentator then explains that this example actually falls under the opposition of contradiction, because the contradictory of anything is its removal, whether positive or negative. He then suggests an alternative wording for the division that would correctly encompass cases of two non-existents: instead of saying 'either both existent or one existent and one non-existent', one should say 'either both existent or not'; then within the non-existent, if it is negation from a receptive subject it is privation-possession, otherwise it is contradiction. This refinement ensures that opposition between two non-existents (like blindness and non-blindness) is not excluded.

Key Terms
عدم
ثبوتي
سَلْبِي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Al-Sa'd establishes that contradictory opposites can both be non-existential, refining the standard division of logical oppositions.

The Four Types of Opposition in Mantiq
Author classifies opposition into four types and refines the division.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and distinguish the four types of opposition (taqābul) as defined in classical mantiq.

Core Idea
Opposition is not monolithic; four types reveal the logical structure of reality.

When we say two things are opposed, what exactly does that mean? In mantiq, opposition is carefully divided into four distinct types based on existential status and conceptual dependency. This lesson walks through that classification, using familiar pairs like father/son, whiteness/blackness, sight/blindness, and blackness/not-blackness. Understanding these types is essential for rigorous reasoning in Islamic theology and jurisprudence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basis of division
The passage starts by stating that opposites are either both existential or one existential and one non-existential. Note this initial split — it is the root of the classification.
Existential means positive, non-existential means negative.
2
Distinguish the two existential types
When both are existential, check if understanding one requires understanding the other. If yes, they are correlatives (e.g., fatherhood and sonhood); if no, they are contraries (e.g., whiteness and blackness).
Correlatives are conceptually interdependent; contraries are not.
3
Distinguish the mixed types
When one is existential and the other non-existential, look at the subject. If the non-existential is absence in a subject capable of having that existential, it is privation/possession (e.g., blindness in a sighted person). If there is no such capacity requirement, it is contradiction (e.g., blackness and its negation).
The same pair can be privation in one subject and mere contradiction in another.
4
Understand the refinement about non-existential contradictories
The commentator notes that al-Sa'd objected to the assumption that both opposites cannot be non-existential. Later logicians accept that the contradictory of a non-existential can be non-existential (e.g., impossibility and non-impossibility). This still falls under contradiction.
This shows the classification is not rigid; it accommodates nuance.

فصل في التناقض وَوَجْهُ الحَصْرِ : أَنَّ المُتَقَابِلَيْنِ : إِمَّا وُجُودِيَّانِ ، أَوْ أَحَدُهُمَا وُجُودِيٌّ وَالآخَرُ عَدَمِيٌّ، فَالوُجُودِيَّانِ إِنْ تَوَقَّفَ تَعَقُلُ أَحَدِهِمَا عَلَى تَعَقُلِ الْآخَرِ كَـ : الأُبُوَّةِ، وَالبُنُوَّةِ فَالمُتَضَايفَانِ، أَوْ لَا كَـ : البَيَاضِ ، وَالسَّوَادِ فَالضَّدَّانِ، وَاللَّذَانِ أَحَدُهُمَا وُجُودِيٌّ وَالآخَرُ عَدَمِيٌّ إِنِ اعْتُبِرَ في العَدَمِيِّ كَوْنُ المَحَلِّ قَابِلا لِلوُجُودِي كَـ : البَصَرِ، وَالعَمَى بِالنِّسْبَةِ إِلَى زَيْدٍ مَثَلاً، بِخِلَافِ الحَائِطِ فَعَدَمٌ وَمَلَكَةٌ ، وَإِنْ لَمْ يُعْتَبَرُ كَـ السَّوَادِ وَنَفْيهِ، فَالنَّقِيضَانِ، وَهَذَا مَبْنِي عَلَى أَنَّ المُتَقَابِلَيْنِ (۱) لَا يَكُونَانِ عَدَمِيْنِ . قَالَ السَّعْدُ : وَلَيْسَ عَلَيْهِ دَلِيلٌ ، وَقَدْ أَطْبَقَ المُتَأخُرُونَ عَلَى أَنَّ نَقِيضُ العَدَمِي يَكُونُ عَدَمِيًّا كَـ : الامْتِنَاعِ وَاللَّا امْتِنَاعِ، وَالعَمَى وَاللَّا عَمَى. اهـ. وَهَذَا دَاخِلٌ فِي تَقَابُلِ التَّناقُضِ ؛ لِأَنَّ نَقِيضَ كُلِّ شَيْءٍ رَفْعُهُ؛ سَوَاءٌ كَانَ ذَلِكَ الشَّيْءُ ثُبُوتِيَّا أَوْ سَلْبِيًّا، فَلَوْ قِيلَ فِي وَجْهِ الحَصْرِ : الأَمْرَانِ إِمَّا وُجُودِيَّانِ أَوْ لَا، وَغَيْرُ الوُجُودِيَّيْنِ إِمَّا تَقَابُلُ أَمْرٍ وَسَلْبُهُ عَنْ مَحَلٍّ يَقْبَلُهُ، فَهُوَ تَقَابُلُ العَدَم وَالمَلَكَةِ، وَإِمَّا تَقَابُلُ أَمْرٍ وَسَلْبُهُ مُطلَقاً ، فَهُوَ تَقَابُلُ التَّناقُضِ لَشَمَلَ مَا ذَكَرَ، وَاللهُ تَعَالَى أَعْلَمُ .
Section on contradiction. The basis of the division: the two opposite things are either both existential, or one is existential and the other non-existential. The two existential: if understanding one depends on understanding the other, like fatherhood and sonhood, then they are correlatives; otherwise, like whiteness and blackness, then they are contraries. The two of which one is existential and the other non-existential: if in the non-existential it is considered that the subject is capable of receiving the existential, like sight and blindness with respect to Zayd for example, unlike the wall, then it is privation and possession; and if not considered, like blackness and its negation, then they are contradictories. This is based on the assumption that the two opposites are not both non-existential. Al-Sa'd said: There is no proof for this, and the later scholars are unanimous that the contradictory of a non-existential is non-existential, like impossibility and non-impossibility, and blindness and non-blindness. This falls under the opposition of contradiction because the contradictory of everything is its removal, whether that thing is positive or negative. So if it were said in the basis of the division: the two things are either both existential or not; and the non-existential pair is either opposition of a thing and its negation from a subject that accepts it, so it is opposition of privation and possession, or opposition of a thing and its negation absolutely, so it is opposition of contradiction, then it would include what he mentioned. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 643

Commentary
This passage defines the four types of opposition (taqābul) and refines the division. It begins by stating the basis of classification: opposites are either both existential (wujūdiyyān) or one existential and one non-existential. The existential pair is then subdivided: if understanding one depends on understanding the other, they are correlatives (mutadāyifān), like father and son; if not, they are contraries (muddāddān), like whiteness and blackness. The mixed pair (one existential, one non-existential) is also subdivided: if the non-existential is considered in relation to a subject capable of receiving the existential, it is privation and possession (ʿadam wa malaka), like blindness in a sighted person; if not, it is contradiction (naqīḍān), like blackness and its negation. The author notes this division assumes opposites cannot both be non-existential, but al-Saʿd (Saʿd al-Dīn al-Taftazānī) objects that later logicians accept that the contradictory of a non-existential may itself be non-existential, e.g., impossibility and non-impossibility. The commentator then argues that this case still falls under contradiction because the contradictory of anything is its removal. He suggests a refined classification that would include such cases.

Checkpoint
In the classification of opposition, which type does the pair 'sight and blindness in a human' belong to?
A) Correlatives
B) Contraries
C) Privation and possession
D) Contradictories

Key Takeaway
Opposition in mantiq is classified into four types based on existential status and subject capacity, with a refined division that accommodates non-existential contradictories.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Classify each of the following pairs into one of the four types of opposition: (a) heat and cold, (b) fatherhood and sonhood, (c) sight and blindness in a human, (d) existence and nonexistence. Justify your answers using the criteria from the passage.
?
Al-Sa'd argues that the contradictory of a non-existential (e.g., impossibility) can be non-existential (non-impossibility). Explain why this still falls under the opposition of contradiction, and how the commentator's refined division accommodates this case.
